Let me think about this. Enemy is attacking for 8 + debuff. 

Options:
1. Bash (2) + Strike (1) = 3 energy, 8 + 2 vuln + 6 = 14 damage, 0 block, take 8 + debuff
2. Strike (1) + Strike (1) + Defend (1) = 3 energy, 12 damage, 5 block, take 3 + debuff
3. Bash (2) + Defend (1) = 3 energy, 8 damage + vuln, 5 block, take 3 + debuff


4. Defend + Defend + Strike = 10 block + 6 damage, take 0 (block 10 vs 8)

Option 4 blocks everything but deals minimal damage, while option 3 sets up vulnerability for later turns. The aggressive bash-strike combo deals the most damage but I'd take the full hit plus whatever debuff the Sludge Spinner applies—at 63 HP that's survivable but the debuff is a real concern.

Let me work through the numbers. If I bash now, I apply vulnerability, making my strikes hit for 9 instead of 6 next turn. With the enemy at 37 HP, a bash plus strike does 14 damage this turn, leaving them at 23, but I take 8 damage plus the debuff. Over two turns I could potentially finish them, whereas playing defensively means I need to grind out 31 more damage over the remaining turns. Bash plus a single defend feels like the right balance—I deal 8 damage, apply vulnerability, and only take 3 damage plus the debuff instead of the full hit.

Actually, I need to clarify how debuffs work in this game. The debuff applies as part of the attack action regardless of whether I block the damage, so blocking doesn't prevent it. That means my priority should be maximizing my own damage output while minimizing what gets through, and bash plus defend accomplishes that better than playing it safe.

Let me reflect on this run and what went wrong, what went right, and what I should remember for future runs.

Key mistakes and lessons:

1. **Deck was too thin on damage**: 13 cards with mostly basic strikes/defends. I removed a Strike early (good) but didn't add enough quality cards. I skipped several card rewards that could have helped.

2. **Living Fog fight was brutal**: The Smoggy debuff (1 skill per turn) combined with the minion spawning made this fight drag out. I should have used potions earlier or been more aggressive. Lost a ton of HP here.


3. **Corpse Slug fight - Ravenous mechanic**: The slugs had a Ravenous power that scaled their Strength by 4 for each corpse they consumed, so killing two slugs meant the survivor gained +8 Strength. I needed to either burst them all down simultaneously or prepare for the exponential scaling threat.

4. **Sewer Clam**: The Plating power grants block each turn but decreases by 1 per turn, so I needed to account for the diminishing defense over time.

5. **HP management was terrible**: I took the Chosen Cheese event for 14 HP early, then Living Fog drained me to 28 HP, rested to 59, got hit down to 30 by the Corpse Slugs, and the Sewer Clam finished me at 7 HP. I should've been more conservative with my health or picked up defensive cards instead.

6. **Potion usage**: The Weak Potion worked well against Living Fog, but the Cure All potion didn't seem to function as expected, and I'm still evaluating how the Radiant Tincture performed.

7. **Card evaluation**: Shrug It Off was my best common, Pommel Strike gave solid damage plus card draw, but Sword Boomerang underperformed in single-target fights. Bloodletting was too risky when I was already low on health—I should've prioritized Blood Wall for its efficient block-to-cost ratio or taken more defensive options overall.

8. **Pathing**: Skipping the Elite at Row 8 was the right call given my low HP, but that low HP came from earlier mistakes, so better deck construction could've let me take it.

9. **Event choices**: Still evaluating my decisions here.

The Chosen Cheese trade-off was questionable—14 HP is steep early on, and the relic's +1 max HP per combat is slow value. I'm also reviewing the enemy patterns I faced: Living Fog summons Gas Bombs and applies Smoggy to limit my skills, Corpse Slug gains Strength by eating dead allies so kill order matters, and Sewer Clam needs quick removal before its Plating and Strength buffs get out of hand. The Cure All potion gave me energy and card draw for burst turns, while Radiant Tincture was particularly strong with its energy generation extending into the next few turns.

# Slay the Spire 2 - Memory File

## Run 1 Summary
**Result**: Defeat at Floor 9 (Sewer Clam) | Ironclad A0
**Cause of death**: Insufficient damage output, too many basic cards, poor HP management. Deck had 13 cards but mostly Strikes/Defends. Couldn't kill Sewer Clam before its Strength scaled to +12.

## Enemy Knowledge
- **Living Fog**: Summons Gas Bombs (10 HP minions, 8 damage attacks). Applies "Smoggy" debuff (only 1 skill per turn!). Minions have MinionPower - die when leader dies. PRIORITY: Kill the leader ASAP. Use potions if needed. Smoggy makes block-heavy hands almost unplayable.
- **Gas Bomb**: 10 HP minions, deal 8 damage. Die when leader dies.
- **Corpse Slug**: Has RavenousPower(4). When ANY enemy dies, ALL slugs eat the corpse → stunned that turn + gain Strength (equal to Ravenous value, so +4 each!). Killing 2 slugs gave the last one +8 Strength. STRATEGY: Either kill all at once or be prepared for massive Strength scaling. Consider focusing one down only if others are debuffing/not attacking.
- **Sewer Clam**: Plating gives block each turn (decreases by 1/turn). Buffs Strength repeatedly. Long fights = death. Need concentrated burst damage or Vulnerable to break through armor + kill fast.
- **Seapunk**: Moderate enemy, applies debuffs. Manageable.
- **Toadpole**: Can buff (Thorns, Strength). Kill the buffer first.

## Card Evaluation (Ironclad)
### Strong picks:
- **Shrug It Off**: Best common skill. 8 block + draw for 1 energy. Always take.
- **Pommel Strike**: Good Strike upgrade. 9 damage + draw for 1 energy. Take early.
- **Bloodletting**: 0 cost, +1 energy. RISKY at low HP (3 HP cost). Take only if deck has sustain or you're healthy. Don't play below 10 HP.

### Mediocre/Skip:
- **Sword Boomerang**: 3x3 random damage. Weak in single-target fights, okay for AoE. Not reliable damage.
- **Tremble**: Worse Vulnerable source than Bash. Skip.
- **Molten Fist**: Exhaust = one-time use. Situational.
- **Perfected Strike**: Only good in Strike-heavy decks (bad strategy).

### Cards I should have taken:
- **Blood Wall**: 16 block for 2 energy + 3 HP cost. Very efficient block card, especially vs high-damage enemies.
- Need more UNCOMMON/RARE damage cards. Don't be too picky early - deck needs damage scaling.

## Strategic Lessons
1. **Deck needs damage scaling badly**: Basic Strikes do 6 damage. Against enemies with 50-80 HP + block, this is way too slow. Prioritize damage cards that scale (Strength sources, high-damage attacks, multi-hit with Strength).
2. **Don't skip too many card rewards**: I skipped cards to stay lean but ended up with insufficient damage. A slightly larger deck with better cards beats a tiny deck of basics.
3. **HP is a resource but don't pay too much early**: Chosen Cheese (-14 HP for +1 max HP/combat) was poor value. That's a lot of HP for very slow returns.
4. **Use potions earlier**: Saved Radiant Tincture and Cure All too long. Use them when fights start going badly, not when you're at 7 HP.
5. **Radiant Tincture is VERY strong**: Extra energy for multiple turns. Use at start of hard fights (not when desperate).
6. **Block math matters**: At 7 HP with 22 incoming, you need 16+ block to survive. Plan ahead - don't end up in this situation.
7. **Smoggy (1 skill/turn) counter**: When this debuff is active, Shrug It Off is the only skill to play. Need attack-heavy hands. Consider this when building deck.
8. **Kill priority in multi-enemy fights**: Kill minion summoners first (Living Fog). For Corpse Slugs, be aware of Ravenous snowball.

## Pathing Principles
- Rest sites before Elites are critical
- Don't take Elites below 50% HP
- Unknown rooms are fine above 60% HP
- Shop access matters for card removal
- Early card removal (Strikes) is high value but don't sacrifice too much HP for it

## General Priority
1. Add 1-2 strong damage cards in first 3 fights
2. Get a Strength source or scaling mechanism
3. Shrug It Off + 1 more good block card for defense
4. Remove Strikes when possible
5. Save potions for fights with 40+ HP enemies or multi-enemy encounters
[MEMORY SAVED]

The Vulnerable route gives me a damage multiplier next turn, but 15 damage now versus 8 damage plus the buff debuff is worth calculating across both turns.

Comparing the two paths: Option A kills A and deals 15 to B, leaving B at 10 HP for an easy finish next turn. Option B deals 8 with Vulnerable, but B survives at 17 HP and I'd need to rely on drawing good cards next turn to capitalize on the debuff. The problem is the Clam scales its damage—if it gains 2 Strength per buff turn, by turn 6 it could be hitting for 14-18 damage, which is dangerous.

I need to be aggressive here. My opening move is to play 2 Strikes and 1 Defend to apply some early pressure while maintaining a defensive posture.

I should keep an eye out for Bloodletting when I draw it—using it early could give me the extra energy to push more damage through before the Clam becomes too threatening. For this turn though, 2 Strikes and 1 Defend is the right call with what I have.

# Slay the Spire 2 - Memory File

## Run 1 Summary
**Result**: Defeat at Floor 9 (Sewer Clam) | Ironclad A0
**Cause of death**: Insufficient damage output, too many basic cards, poor HP management. Deck had 13 cards but mostly Strikes/Defends. Couldn't kill Sewer Clam before its Strength scaled to +12.

## Enemy Knowledge
- **Living Fog**: Summons Gas Bombs (10 HP minions, 8 damage attacks). Applies "Smoggy" debuff (only 1 skill per turn!). Minions have MinionPower - die when leader dies. PRIORITY: Kill the leader ASAP. Use potions if needed. Smoggy makes block-heavy hands almost unplayable.
- **Gas Bomb**: 10 HP minions, deal 8 damage. Die when leader dies.
- **Corpse Slug**: Has RavenousPower(4). When ANY enemy dies, ALL slugs eat the corpse → stunned that turn + gain Strength (equal to Ravenous value, so +4 each!). Killing 2 slugs gave the last one +8 Strength. STRATEGY: Either kill all at once or be prepared for massive Strength scaling. Consider focusing one down only if others are debuffing/not attacking.
- **Sewer Clam**: Plating gives block each turn (decreases by 1/turn). Buffs Strength repeatedly. Long fights = death. Need concentrated burst damage or Vulnerable to break through armor + kill fast.
- **Seapunk**: Moderate enemy, applies debuffs. Manageable.
- **Toadpole**: Can buff (Thorns, Strength). Kill the buffer first.

## Card Evaluation (Ironclad)
### Strong picks:
- **Shrug It Off**: Best common skill. 8 block + draw for 1 energy. Always take.
- **Pommel Strike**: Good Strike upgrade. 9 damage + draw for 1 energy. Take early.
- **Bloodletting**: 0 cost, +1 energy. RISKY at low HP (3 HP cost). Take only if deck has sustain or you're healthy. Don't play below 10 HP.

### Mediocre/Skip:
- **Sword Boomerang**: 3x3 random damage. Weak in single-target fights, okay for AoE. Not reliable damage.
- **Tremble**: Worse Vulnerable source than Bash. Skip.
- **Molten Fist**: Exhaust = one-time use. Situational.
- **Perfected Strike**: Only good in Strike-heavy decks (bad strategy).

### Cards I should have taken:
- **Blood Wall**: 16 block for 2 energy + 3 HP cost. Very efficient block card, especially vs high-damage enemies.
- Need more UNCOMMON/RARE damage cards. Don't be too picky early - deck needs damage scaling.

## Strategic Lessons
1. **Deck needs damage scaling badly**: Basic Strikes do 6 damage. Against enemies with 50-80 HP + block, this is way too slow. Prioritize damage cards that scale (Strength sources, high-damage attacks, multi-hit with Strength).
2. **Don't skip too many card rewards**: I skipped cards to stay lean but ended up with insufficient damage. A slightly larger deck with better cards beats a tiny deck of basics.
3. **HP is a resource but don't pay too much early**: Chosen Cheese (-14 HP for +1 max HP/combat) was poor value. That's a lot of HP for very slow returns.
4. **Use potions earlier**: Saved Radiant Tincture and Cure All too long. Use them when fights start going badly, not when you're at 7 HP.
5. **Radiant Tincture is VERY strong**: Extra energy for multiple turns. Use at start of hard fights (not when desperate).
6. **Block math matters**: At 7 HP with 22 incoming, you need 16+ block to survive. Plan ahead - don't end up in this situation.
7. **Smoggy (1 skill/turn) counter**: When this debuff is active, Shrug It Off is the only skill to play. Need attack-heavy hands. Consider this when building deck.
8. **Kill priority in multi-enemy fights**: Kill minion summoners first (Living Fog). For Corpse Slugs, be aware of Ravenous snowball.

## Pathing Principles
- Rest sites before Elites are critical
- Don't take Elites below 50% HP
- Unknown rooms are fine above 60% HP
- Shop access matters for card removal
- Early card removal (Strikes) is high value but don't sacrifice too much HP for it

## General Priority
1. Add 1-2 strong damage cards in first 3 fights
2. Get a Strength source or scaling mechanism
3. Shrug It Off + 1 more good block card for defense
4. Remove Strikes when possible
5. Save potions for fights with 40+ HP enemies or multi-enemy encounters

# Slay the Spire 2 - Memory File

## Run Summaries
**Run 1**: Defeat at Floor 9 (Sewer Clam) | Ironclad A0. Insufficient damage, too many basics.
**Run 2**: Defeat at Floor 9 (Terror Eel Elite) | Ironclad A0. Entered Elite at 35 HP, got hit by 17 unblocked T1 (Radiant Tincture didn't give energy immediately?), then 24 damage turn brought me to 2 HP. Vulnerable 99 debuff from eel made any hit lethal. Deck was better (15 cards, Rage/Bloodletting/2x Pommel/Shrug/Blood Wall) but HP management was fatal.

## Enemy Knowledge
- **Living Fog**: Summons Gas Bombs (10 HP minions, 8 damage). Applies "Smoggy" (only 1 skill/turn). Minions die when leader dies. PRIORITY: Kill leader ASAP. Smoggy makes block-heavy hands terrible.
- **Gas Bomb**: 10 HP minions, 8 damage. Die when leader dies.
- **Corpse Slug**: RavenousPower(4). When any enemy dies, all slugs eat corpse → stunned that turn + gain Strength (+4 each). Strategy: Focus one down, use stun window to damage others. Killed A → B stunned → free turn. Repeat. Be aware last slug has huge Strength.
- **Sewer Clam**: Plating block each turn (decreases by 1). Buffs Strength repeatedly. Long fights = death. Need burst + Vulnerable.
- **Seapunk**: Moderate. Attacks + buffs. Manageable.
- **Toadpole**: Buffs (Thorns +2, Strength). Kill the buffer first. Thorns = 2 damage per attack hit.
- **Sludge Spinner**: Attacks + applies Weak. Buffs Strength. Kill before it scales.
- **Terror Eel (ELITE)**: 140 HP. ShriekPower(70) = when first drops to ≤50% HP, gets STUNNED. VigorPower buffs next attack. Applies Vulnerable 99 via debuff turn. HUGE damage swings (17 base, 24+ with Vigor). STRATEGY: Rush to 70 HP threshold for free stun turn. Must block PERFECTLY after Vulnerable 99 applied - any hit is near-lethal. Use potions turn 1. This fight requires high sustained DPS + reliable block.

## Card Evaluation (Ironclad)
### Strong:
- **Shrug It Off**: Best common skill. 8 block + draw for 1 energy. Always take.
- **Pommel Strike**: 9 damage + draw for 1 energy. Strict upgrade to Strike. Always take.
- **Rage**: 0 cost, +3 block per attack played this turn. AMAZING with attack-heavy turns. Rage + 3 attacks = 9 free block. Synergizes with Bloodletting (more energy = more attacks = more Rage block).
- **Blood Wall**: 16 block for 2 energy + 2 HP cost. Very efficient. DON'T play at ≤2 HP.
- **Bloodletting**: 0 cost, +1 energy, -3 HP. Strong in healthy state. NEVER play at ≤3 HP.

### Mediocre/Skip:
- **Sword Boomerang**: 3x3 random. Unreliable.
- **Tremble**: Worse Vulnerable than Bash. Skip.
- **Molten Fist**: Exhaust = one-use. Situational.
- **Perfected Strike**: Trap card. Gets worse as you remove Strikes.
- **Setup Strike**: 7 damage + 2 temp Strength. Mediocre.
- **Bully**: 4 damage + bonus per Vulnerable. Too conditional.

### HIGH PRIORITY NEEDS:
- **Strength scaling**: Demon Form, Inflame, Limit Break, Spot Weakness - ANY permanent Strength source
- **AOE damage**: For multi-enemy fights
- **Uncommon/Rare damage cards**: Carnage, Uppercut, Clothesline, etc.

## Potion Knowledge
- **Radiant Tincture**: Gives energy NOW + extra energy for next N turns. Use at START of hard fights (turn 1).
- **Cure All**: Gives energy + draws 2 cards. Use when you need both cards and energy in same turn.
- **Weak Potion**: 3 Weak. Good for reducing big attacks by 25%.
- **CRITICAL LESSON**: Potions are FREE actions. Use them BEFORE playing cards to maximize options. Use offensive potions early in Elite/Boss fights, not when desperate.

## Strategic Lessons (Updated)
1. **HP management is #1 priority**: Both runs died because HP was too low entering critical fights. Run 2: 35 HP into Elite = death.
2. **DON'T enter Elites below 50% HP**: Run 2 had 35/80 (44%) going into Terror Eel. Should have found a way to heal more or avoid the Elite.
3. **Pathing with forced Elites is dangerous**: Run 2 had only one path leading to Elite with no alternative. Check map carefully - avoid paths that force Elites without rest site access.
4. **Use potions on Turn 1 of hard fights**: Radiant Tincture on T1 of Terror Eel was correct. But I should have used it even before the Elite - maybe during the Living Fog fight to preserve HP.
5. **Block math is life-or-death**: At 2 HP with 25 incoming and Vulnerable 99, you're dead. Never let HP get this low. The Terror Eel's Vulnerable 99 makes you take 50% more damage - factor this into block math.
6. **Rage is incredible for simultaneous offense/defense**: Rage + Bloodletting + attacks = damage + block in same turn. Build around this.
7. **Don't be greedy on attack turns when HP is low**: Run 2 T1 vs Terror Eel: I played Bash + Pommel (21 damage) but took 17 unblocked. Should have blocked more and dealt less damage.
8. **Blood Wall and Bloodletting have HP costs**: Don't take these into fights at low HP. They become dead cards.
9. **Deck was still too Strike-heavy**: 4 Strikes in a 15-card deck. Should buy removal at shops or take more upgrades over basics.

## Pathing Principles (Updated)
- REST before Elites - NON-NEGOTIABLE
- Don't take Elites below 55% HP even with potions
- Shop > Unknown when you need card removal
- Check ALL paths from current position before committing - avoid paths that force Elites without healing
- Early fights: prioritize getting hit less over dealing more damage. HP entering Elite matters more than killing trash 1 turn faster.

## Turn-by-Turn Combat Priorities
1. Check incoming damage FIRST
2. Calculate: can I block all/most of it?
3. If HP ≤ 20: block is almost always priority over damage
4. If enemy is buffing (no attack): go all-in on damage
5. Use Rage early in turn, then play attacks
6. Bloodletting only when HP > 15 and you need the extra energy
7. Save Bash for when Vulnerable will matter (high HP enemies, multi-turn benefit)

## General Deck Building Priority
1. Add 1-2 Pommel Strikes early (replace Strikes functionally)
2. Get Strength scaling (Demon Form, Inflame, etc.) - THIS IS CRITICAL
3. Shrug It Off for defense + cycle
4. Rage for attack/defense synergy
5. Remove Strikes at shops (75g well spent)
6. Don't bloat deck past ~18 cards without good reason
[MEMORY SAVED]

# Slay the Spire 2 - Memory File

## Run Summaries
**Run 1**: Defeat at Floor 9 (Sewer Clam) | Ironclad A0. Insufficient damage, too many basics.
**Run 2**: Defeat at Floor 9 (Terror Eel Elite) | Ironclad A0. Entered Elite at 35 HP, got hit by 17 unblocked T1 (Radiant Tincture didn't give energy immediately?), then 24 damage turn brought me to 2 HP. Vulnerable 99 debuff from eel made any hit lethal. Deck was better (15 cards, Rage/Bloodletting/2x Pommel/Shrug/Blood Wall) but HP management was fatal.

## Enemy Knowledge
- **Living Fog**: Summons Gas Bombs (10 HP minions, 8 damage). Applies "Smoggy" (only 1 skill/turn). Minions die when leader dies. PRIORITY: Kill leader ASAP. Smoggy makes block-heavy hands terrible.
- **Gas Bomb**: 10 HP minions, 8 damage. Die when leader dies.
- **Corpse Slug**: RavenousPower(4). When any enemy dies, all slugs eat corpse → stunned that turn + gain Strength (+4 each). Strategy: Focus one down, use stun window to damage others. Killed A → B stunned → free turn. Repeat. Be aware last slug has huge Strength.
- **Sewer Clam**: Plating block each turn (decreases by 1). Buffs Strength repeatedly. Long fights = death. Need burst + Vulnerable.
- **Seapunk**: Moderate. Attacks + buffs. Manageable.
- **Toadpole**: Buffs (Thorns +2, Strength). Kill the buffer first. Thorns = 2 damage per attack hit.
- **Sludge Spinner**: Attacks + applies Weak. Buffs Strength. Kill before it scales.
- **Terror Eel (ELITE)**: 140 HP. ShriekPower(70) = when first drops to ≤50% HP, gets STUNNED. VigorPower buffs next attack. Applies Vulnerable 99 via debuff turn. HUGE damage swings (17 base, 24+ with Vigor). STRATEGY: Rush to 70 HP threshold for free stun turn. Must block PERFECTLY after Vulnerable 99 applied - any hit is near-lethal. Use potions turn 1. This fight requires high sustained DPS + reliable block.

## Card Evaluation (Ironclad)
### Strong:
- **Shrug It Off**: Best common skill. 8 block + draw for 1 energy. Always take.
- **Pommel Strike**: 9 damage + draw for 1 energy. Strict upgrade to Strike. Always take.
- **Rage**: 0 cost, +3 block per attack played this turn. AMAZING with attack-heavy turns. Rage + 3 attacks = 9 free block. Synergizes with Bloodletting (more energy = more attacks = more Rage block).
- **Blood Wall**: 16 block for 2 energy + 2 HP cost. Very efficient. DON'T play at ≤2 HP.
- **Bloodletting**: 0 cost, +1 energy, -3 HP. Strong in healthy state. NEVER play at ≤3 HP.

### Mediocre/Skip:
- **Sword Boomerang**: 3x3 random. Unreliable.
- **Tremble**: Worse Vulnerable than Bash. Skip.
- **Molten Fist**: Exhaust = one-use. Situational.
- **Perfected Strike**: Trap card. Gets worse as you remove Strikes.
- **Setup Strike**: 7 damage + 2 temp Strength. Mediocre.
- **Bully**: 4 damage + bonus per Vulnerable. Too conditional.

### HIGH PRIORITY NEEDS:
- **Strength scaling**: Demon Form, Inflame, Limit Break, Spot Weakness - ANY permanent Strength source
- **AOE damage**: For multi-enemy fights
- **Uncommon/Rare damage cards**: Carnage, Uppercut, Clothesline, etc.

## Potion Knowledge
- **Radiant Tincture**: Gives energy NOW + extra energy for next N turns. Use at START of hard fights (turn 1).
- **Cure All**: Gives energy + draws 2 cards. Use when you need both cards and energy in same turn.
- **Weak Potion**: 3 Weak. Good for reducing big attacks by 25%.
- **CRITICAL LESSON**: Potions are FREE actions. Use them BEFORE playing cards to maximize options. Use offensive potions early in Elite/Boss fights, not when desperate.

## Strategic Lessons (Updated)
1. **HP management is #1 priority**: Both runs died because HP was too low entering critical fights. Run 2: 35 HP into Elite = death.
2. **DON'T enter Elites below 50% HP**: Run 2 had 35/80 (44%) going into Terror Eel. Should have found a way to heal more or avoid the Elite.
3. **Pathing with forced Elites is dangerous**: Run 2 had only one path leading to Elite with no alternative. Check map carefully - avoid paths that force Elites without rest site access.
4. **Use potions on Turn 1 of hard fights**: Radiant Tincture on T1 of Terror Eel was correct. But I should have used it even before the Elite - maybe during the Living Fog fight to preserve HP.
5. **Block math is life-or-death**: At 2 HP with 25 incoming and Vulnerable 99, you're dead. Never let HP get this low. The Terror Eel's Vulnerable 99 makes you take 50% more damage - factor this into block math.
6. **Rage is incredible for simultaneous offense/defense**: Rage + Bloodletting + attacks = damage + block in same turn. Build around this.
7. **Don't be greedy on attack turns when HP is low**: Run 2 T1 vs Terror Eel: I played Bash + Pommel (21 damage) but took 17 unblocked. Should have blocked more and dealt less damage.
8. **Blood Wall and Bloodletting have HP costs**: Don't take these into fights at low HP. They become dead cards.
9. **Deck was still too Strike-heavy**: 4 Strikes in a 15-card deck. Should buy removal at shops or take more upgrades over basics.

## Pathing Principles (Updated)
- REST before Elites - NON-NEGOTIABLE
- Don't take Elites below 55% HP even with potions
- Shop > Unknown when you need card removal
- Check ALL paths from current position before committing - avoid paths that force Elites without healing
- Early fights: prioritize getting hit less over dealing more damage. HP entering Elite matters more than killing trash 1 turn faster.

## Turn-by-Turn Combat Priorities
1. Check incoming damage FIRST
2. Calculate: can I block all/most of it?
3. If HP ≤ 20: block is almost always priority over damage
4. If enemy is buffing (no attack): go all-in on damage
5. Use Rage early in turn, then play attacks
6. Bloodletting only when HP > 15 and you need the extra energy
7. Save Bash for when Vulnerable will matter (high HP enemies, multi-turn benefit)

## General Deck Building Priority
1. Add 1-2 Pommel Strikes early (replace Strikes functionally)
2. Get Strength scaling (Demon Form, Inflame, etc.) - THIS IS CRITICAL
3. Shrug It Off for defense + cycle
4. Rage for attack/defense synergy
5. Remove Strikes at shops (75g well spent)
6. Don't bloat deck past ~18 cards without good reason

# Slay the Spire 2 - Memory File

## Run Summaries
**Run 1**: Defeat at Floor 9 (Sewer Clam) | Ironclad A0. Insufficient damage, too many basics.
**Run 2**: Defeat at Floor 9 (Terror Eel Elite) | Ironclad A0. Entered Elite at 35 HP, got hit by 17 unblocked T1 (Radiant Tincture didn't give energy immediately?), then 24 damage turn brought me to 2 HP. Vulnerable 99 debuff from eel made any hit lethal. Deck was better (15 cards, Rage/Bloodletting/2x Pommel/Shrug/Blood Wall) but HP management was fatal.

## Enemy Knowledge
- **Living Fog**: Summons Gas Bombs (10 HP minions, 8 damage). Applies "Smoggy" (only 1 skill/turn). Minions die when leader dies. PRIORITY: Kill leader ASAP. Smoggy makes block-heavy hands terrible.
- **Gas Bomb**: 10 HP minions, 8 damage. Die when leader dies.
- **Corpse Slug**: RavenousPower(4). When any enemy dies, all slugs eat corpse → stunned that turn + gain Strength (+4 each). Strategy: Focus one down, use stun window to damage others. Killed A → B stunned → free turn. Repeat. Be aware last slug has huge Strength.
- **Sewer Clam**: Plating block each turn (decreases by 1). Buffs Strength repeatedly. Long fights = death. Need burst + Vulnerable.
- **Seapunk**: Moderate. Attacks + buffs. Manageable.
- **Toadpole**: Buffs (Thorns +2, Strength). Kill the buffer first. Thorns = 2 damage per attack hit.
- **Sludge Spinner**: Attacks + applies Weak. Buffs Strength. Kill before it scales.
- **Terror Eel (ELITE)**: 140 HP. ShriekPower(70) = when first drops to ≤50% HP, gets STUNNED. VigorPower buffs next attack. Applies Vulnerable 99 via debuff turn. HUGE damage swings (17 base, 24+ with Vigor). STRATEGY: Rush to 70 HP threshold for free stun turn. Must block PERFECTLY after Vulnerable 99 applied - any hit is near-lethal. Use potions turn 1. This fight requires high sustained DPS + reliable block.

## Card Evaluation (Ironclad)
### Strong:
- **Shrug It Off**: Best common skill. 8 block + draw for 1 energy. Always take.
- **Pommel Strike**: 9 damage + draw for 1 energy. Strict upgrade to Strike. Always take.
- **Rage**: 0 cost, +3 block per attack played this turn. AMAZING with attack-heavy turns. Rage + 3 attacks = 9 free block. Synergizes with Bloodletting (more energy = more attacks = more Rage block).
- **Blood Wall**: 16 block for 2 energy + 2 HP cost. Very efficient. DON'T play at ≤2 HP.
- **Bloodletting**: 0 cost, +1 energy, -3 HP. Strong in healthy state. NEVER play at ≤3 HP.

### Mediocre/Skip:
- **Sword Boomerang**: 3x3 random. Unreliable.
- **Tremble**: Worse Vulnerable than Bash. Skip.
- **Molten Fist**: Exhaust = one-use. Situational.
- **Perfected Strike**: Trap card. Gets worse as you remove Strikes.
- **Setup Strike**: 7 damage + 2 temp Strength. Mediocre.
- **Bully**: 4 damage + bonus per Vulnerable. Too conditional.

### HIGH PRIORITY NEEDS:
- **Strength scaling**: Demon Form, Inflame, Limit Break, Spot Weakness - ANY permanent Strength source
- **AOE damage**: For multi-enemy fights
- **Uncommon/Rare damage cards**: Carnage, Uppercut, Clothesline, etc.

## Potion Knowledge
- **Radiant Tincture**: Gives energy NOW + extra energy for next N turns. Use at START of hard fights (turn 1).
- **Cure All**: Gives energy + draws 2 cards. Use when you need both cards and energy in same turn.
- **Weak Potion**: 3 Weak. Good for reducing big attacks by 25%.
- **CRITICAL LESSON**: Potions are FREE actions. Use them BEFORE playing cards to maximize options. Use offensive potions early in Elite/Boss fights, not when desperate.

## Strategic Lessons (Updated)
1. **HP management is #1 priority**: Both runs died because HP was too low entering critical fights. Run 2: 35 HP into Elite = death.
2. **DON'T enter Elites below 50% HP**: Run 2 had 35/80 (44%) going into Terror Eel. Should have found a way to heal more or avoid the Elite.
3. **Pathing with forced Elites is dangerous**: Run 2 had only one path leading to Elite with no alternative. Check map carefully - avoid paths that force Elites without rest site access.
4. **Use potions on Turn 1 of hard fights**: Radiant Tincture on T1 of Terror Eel was correct. But I should have used it even before the Elite - maybe during the Living Fog fight to preserve HP.
5. **Block math is life-or-death**: At 2 HP with 25 incoming and Vulnerable 99, you're dead. Never let HP get this low. The Terror Eel's Vulnerable 99 makes you take 50% more damage - factor this into block math.
6. **Rage is incredible for simultaneous offense/defense**: Rage + Bloodletting + attacks = damage + block in same turn. Build around this.
7. **Don't be greedy on attack turns when HP is low**: Run 2 T1 vs Terror Eel: I played Bash + Pommel (21 damage) but took 17 unblocked. Should have blocked more and dealt less damage.
8. **Blood Wall and Bloodletting have HP costs**: Don't take these into fights at low HP. They become dead cards.
9. **Deck was still too Strike-heavy**: 4 Strikes in a 15-card deck. Should buy removal at shops or take more upgrades over basics.

## Pathing Principles (Updated)
- REST before Elites - NON-NEGOTIABLE
- Don't take Elites below 55% HP even with potions
- Shop > Unknown when you need card removal
- Check ALL paths from current position before committing - avoid paths that force Elites without healing
- Early fights: prioritize getting hit less over dealing more damage. HP entering Elite matters more than killing trash 1 turn faster.

## Turn-by-Turn Combat Priorities
1. Check incoming damage FIRST
2. Calculate: can I block all/most of it?
3. If HP ≤ 20: block is almost always priority over damage
4. If enemy is buffing (no attack): go all-in on damage
5. Use Rage early in turn, then play attacks
6. Bloodletting only when HP > 15 and you need the extra energy
7. Save Bash for when Vulnerable will matter (high HP enemies, multi-turn benefit)

## General Deck Building Priority
1. Add 1-2 Pommel Strikes early (replace Strikes functionally)
2. Get Strength scaling (Demon Form, Inflame, etc.) - THIS IS CRITICAL
3. Shrug It Off for defense + cycle
4. Rage for attack/defense synergy
5. Remove Strikes at shops (75g well spent)
6. Don't bloat deck past ~18 cards without good reason

Hmm, maybe "3/3" is the MAX and potions add temporary energy above max. So I had 3+potion energy = maybe 5, spent 1 on Pommel = 4? But display shows 2/3. That's weird.

Wait, actually I said the commands out of order. Let me re-read my actual move:

I said: "POTION P2, POTION P1, PLAY 2, PLAY 3 -> A"

Card [2] was Rage (0 cost), Card [3] was Pommel Strike (1 cost). Total energy spent: 1. If I started with 3, I should have 2. That matches 2/3.

But the potions should have given energy too! Unless they don't... Hmm.

Then the next system prompt showed me with 4 cards and Energy 0/3. But I then said "POTION P1, PLAY 1 -> A, PLAY 2 -> A, PLAY 4 -> A"

Wait, I still had P1 (Cure All)? But I already used it! Unless the system didn't process my potion commands properly because I mixed them with PLAY commands.

Actually, I think what happened is my first message with "POTION P2, POTION P1, PLAY 2, PLAY 3 -> A" might not have fully resolved the potions before playing cards, so maybe the system only registered the card plays and ignored the potion commands, or processed them in a way that didn't add energy as expected. The potions either weren't processed or give zero energy—the Cure All description has unfilled placeholders, which suggests the energy value might be broken or genuinely zero. Looking back at turn 1 when I used Radiant Tincture, I had enough energy for plays that exceeded my base 3, so that potion likely did grant energy, but I need to figure out why Cure All didn't work the same way.

The real problem is I died, and examining that critical turn with 25 damage incoming, I need to trace through what block I actually had available—Rage should've given 3 block per attack, but I'm not certain how many attacks I could play with the hand Cure All gave me. I see the third Strike couldn't be played due to zero energy, so I only dealt 9 block against 25 incoming damage, taking 16 damage and surviving at 1 HP. Next turn I finished the Eel with Pommel and Strike, but the game registered me as dead—maybe the Eel's Vulnerable debuff on me had a longer duration than I thought. So the displayed damage of 12 was already accounting for my Vulnerability—meaning my Pommel Strike and Strike should've killed the eel before it could attack, but something went wrong. I'm going to move past this confusion and extract what I learned: I entered the Elite fight with dangerously low HP (41/80), and the earlier fights against Corpse Slug and Sewer Clam wore me down too much, especially since I didn't block effectively on the first turn against Corpse Slug.

The real pattern across all three runs is clear—I keep arriving at the Elite underprepared, and my deck is bloated with too many basic Strikes and Defends when I should've used the shop to trim it down. Rage combos are powerful for offense and defense simultaneously, but I need to lean harder into attacks and lighter on defense, plus I never even visited the shop despite having 176 gold available.

For the Terror Eel specifically, I need to recognize that the stun at 50% HP is the turning point—rushing to trigger it gives me a window where the Eel's debuffs actually work in my favor for two turns of free damage, but I have to survive the Vulnerable phase afterward with enough block ready.

Looking back at Run 3, the math on that final turn doesn't add up: I took 25 damage with Vulnerable 99, which minus my 9 block should've left me at 1 HP, but somehow I still lost. Either the displayed HP was incorrect or there's a damage calculation I'm missing—possibly the Eel's buff modifier stacks differently than I thought. Vigor which then hits me? No, that's for next attack.

Actually, I wonder if Blood Wall's "lose 2 HP" part kills you if you're at 1 HP. But I didn't play Blood Wall on the last turn. 

I think the most likely explanation is: maybe Radiant Tincture's "energy at start of turn" did something weird, or maybe I miscounted block somewhere, or maybe there's a thorns/reflect mechanic I missed.

Regardless, let me update the memory with practical lessons.

Actually, rethinking - maybe the game killed me because of potion interaction. When I used Cure All at 1 HP... does Cure All cost HP? The description says "获得{Energy:energyIcons()}。抽{Cards}张牌。" - no HP cost mentioned. So that's not it.

Or maybe the Radiant Tincture wasn't consumed properly by the system, since the potion list still showed it even after I used it earlier. This is confusing.

Let me just accept the death and focus on what I can learn. One more thought though - I issued multiple commands on the same turn (potions and card plays), and maybe the system only processed until it hit something it couldn't handle. The energy and block values after my plays suggest the potions might not have actually resolved, so I'm probably miscounting what resources I actually had available.

The key takeaway: potions seem to give variable or zero energy based on the placeholder text, so I shouldn't rely on them for energy calculations. I should use them for card draws and effects instead.

Now let me update the memory file with these insights. But first, I'm reconsidering the path choice - I took Rest at (6,3) instead of Shop at (6,2). The Rest path goes to an Elite at (8,3), while Shop could have led to either an Elite at (8,0) or a Monster at (8,2). If I'd gone Shop → (7,1) → (8,2), I could have avoided the Elite entirely.

This was a critical mistake. I prioritized healing over pathing flexibility when I should have gone to the Shop, used my 176 gold for card removal, and taken the safer Monster path. # Slay the Spire 2 - Memory File

## Run Summaries
**Run 1**: Defeat Floor 9 (Sewer Clam) | Ironclad A0. Insufficient damage, too many basics.
**Run 2**: Defeat Floor 9 (Terror Eel Elite) | Ironclad A0. Entered Elite at 35 HP. Vulnerable 99 made any hit lethal.
**Run 3**: Defeat Floor 9 (Terror Eel Elite) | Ironclad A0. Entered Elite at 41 HP (51%). Had good deck (Rage/Bloodletting/2xPommel/Shrug/BloodWall) + 3 potions. Got Eel to 16 HP at 1 HP but died. **CRITICAL PATHING ERROR**: Chose RestSite(6,3) which FORCED Elite path. Should have chosen Shop(6,2) which allowed avoiding Elite via (7,1)→(8,2) Monster route. Healing was less important than path flexibility.

## Enemy Knowledge
- **Living Fog**: 80 HP. Summons Gas Bombs (10 HP, 8 damage). Applies "Smoggy" (1 skill/turn). Minions die when leader dies. KILL LEADER ASAP. With Smoggy, prioritize attacks over skills.
- **Gas Bomb**: 10 HP minions, 8 damage. Die when leader dies.
- **Corpse Slug**: RavenousPower(4). When enemy dies, remaining slugs eat corpse → stunned + gain 4 Strength each. Chain-kill strategy works but last slug has MASSIVE Strength. Block T1 even if it delays chain - don't take 14 unblocked.
- **Sewer Clam**: 56 HP. Plating block (starts 8, decreases by 1/turn). Buffs Strength +4 repeatedly. Long fights = death. Need burst + Vulnerable. Bash through Plating is inefficient (8 dmg vs 8 block = 0 HP damage). Need to outpace Plating with multi-attack turns or Vulnerable.
- **Seapunk**: 45 HP. Moderate. Attacks + buffs Strength. Manageable.
- **Toadpole**: Buffs (Thorns +2, Strength). Kill the buffer first. Thorns = 2 per attack hit. Shrug It Off for block absorbs Thorns.
- **Sludge Spinner**: 37 HP. Attacks + applies Weak + buffs Strength. Kill fast.
- **Terror Eel (ELITE)**: 140 HP. ShriekPower(70) = STUNNED when first drops to ≤50% HP. VigorPower buffs next attack. Applies Vulnerable 99 via 2 debuff turns after stun. Post-Vuln attacks hit 25+ (displayed number INCLUDES your Vulnerability). STRATEGY: Rush to 70 HP → free stun turn → 2 debuff turns (free damage) → MUST block perfectly after Vuln99. Need ~68 damage in 4-5 turns to trigger stun, then finish remaining 70 HP with 2 free turns + careful blocking.

## Card Evaluation (Ironclad)
### Strong (Always Take):
- **Shrug It Off**: 8 block + draw for 1 energy. Best common skill.
- **Pommel Strike**: 9 damage + draw for 1 energy. Strict upgrade to Strike.
- **Rage**: 0 cost, +3 block per attack this turn. AMAZING with attack-heavy hands + Bloodletting.
- **Bloodletting**: 0 cost, +1 energy, -3 HP. Enables big turns. NEVER play at ≤3 HP.

### Situational:
- **Blood Wall**: 16 block for 2 energy + 2 HP. Efficient but HP cost dangerous at low HP. Good in healthy state.
- **Pillage**: 6 damage + draw until non-attack. Interesting with attack-heavy builds - could chain into more attacks.

### Skip:
- **Sword Boomerang**: 3x3 random. Unreliable.
- **Tremble**: Worse Vulnerable than Bash.
- **Molten Fist**: Exhaust = one-use. Skip.
- **Perfected Strike**: Trap card. Gets worse with Strike removal.
- **Setup Strike**: 7 damage + 2 temp Strength. Mediocre.
- **Bully**: 4 damage + bonus per Vulnerable. Too conditional.

### HIGH PRIORITY NEEDS:
- **Strength scaling**: Demon Form, Inflame, Limit Break, Spot Weakness - ANY permanent Strength source. ALL 3 RUNS lacked this.
- **AOE damage**: Multi-enemy fights are HP drains without it.
- **Uncommon/Rare damage**: Carnage, Uppercut, Clothesline, etc.
- **Card removal**: Remove Strikes at shops. 75g well spent.

## Potion Knowledge
- **Radiant Tincture**: "获得{Energy}。在你的下N个回合开始时，额外获得1能量。" Use T1 of hard fights. NOTE: Placeholder text unclear on exact energy amounts - don't over-rely on potion energy math.
- **Cure All**: "获得{Energy}。抽2张牌。" Draws + possible energy. Use for card access in critical moments.
- **Weak Potion**: 3 Weak. Reduces attacks 25%. Use T1 vs big hitters to reduce damage for 3 turns.
- **CRITICAL**: Potions are FREE actions. Always use BEFORE playing cards.

## Strategic Lessons (KEY - All 3 Runs)
### #1: PATHING IS MORE IMPORTANT THAN HEALING
- Run 3's fatal mistake: Chose RestSite over Shop when Shop path AVOIDED the Elite entirely. Always check where paths lead before choosing rest/shop/unknown.
- Rest that forces you into Elite > Shop that lets you avoid Elite.

### #2: HP Management
- All 3 runs died entering Elite at 35-41 HP (44-51%). Need 60%+ HP (48+ for 80 max).
- Use potions in regular fights to PRESERVE HP for Elite, not save them all.
- Living Fog + Corpse Slugs drained 39 HP in Run 3. Could have used Weak Potion on Corpse Slugs T1 to save 5-8 HP.

### #3: Avoid Forced Elites
- If a path forces you through an Elite with no alternative, DON'T take it unless you're at 70%+ HP with potions.
- Shop paths often branch more than Rest paths.

### #4: Block First, Damage Second at Low HP
- At ≤20 HP: ALWAYS block over damage. Period.
- At 20-40 HP: Block incoming fully, deal damage only with leftover energy.
- At 40+ HP: Can afford aggression if it speeds up kill.

### #5: Don't Be Greedy T1 Against Attackers
- Run 3 T1 vs Corpse Slugs: All-in damage, took 14 unblocked. Should have blocked + dealt less damage.
- Run 2 & 3 T1 vs Terror Eel: Went offensive, took 10-12+ unblocked.

### #6: Use Potions Earlier
- Weak Potion on Corpse Slug T1 saves ~5 HP over fight.
- Radiant Tincture on Sewer Clam (scaling enemy) could shorten fight by 2 turns = save 10+ HP.
- Entering Elite at higher HP is worth more than having potions at low HP.

## Combat Priorities (Turn-by-Turn)
1. Check incoming damage FIRST
2. Calculate: can I block all of it?
3. If HP ≤ 20: block is ALWAYS priority
4. If HP ≤ 40: block fully, damage with leftover
5. If enemy is buffing (no attack): go all-in on damage
6. Use Rage BEFORE attacks (0 cost)
7. Use Pommel Strike for draw before committing remaining energy
8. Bloodletting only when HP > 15
9. Blood Wall only when HP > 10
10. Save Bash for high-HP enemies where Vulnerable pays off over 2+ turns

## Deck Building Priority
1. Pommel Strike x2 early (replace Strikes)
2. Shrug It Off for defense + cycle
3. Strength scaling (CRITICAL NEED - 0/3 runs found any)
4. Rage for attack/defense synergy
5. Remove Strikes at shops (75g, very high priority)
6. Don't bloat past ~17 cards
7. Need more uncommon/rare damage cards

## Pathing Principles (REVISED - CRITICAL)
1. **CHECK ALL DOWNSTREAM PATHS** before choosing a room. A rest site that forces Elite is WORSE than a shop that avoids it.
2. Shop > Rest when: you have gold for removal AND shop path avoids Elite
3. Rest before Elite ONLY if you're already committed to Elite path
4. Don't take Elites below 60% HP
5. Use potions in hallway fights to preserve HP - don't hoard all for Elite
6. Ideal pre-Elite path: Monster → Monster → Shop(remove) → Rest → Elite
7. If possible, avoid Elites in Act 1 entirely until deck has scaling
[MEMORY SAVED]

# Slay the Spire 2 - Memory File

## Run Summaries
**Run 1**: Defeat Floor 9 (Sewer Clam) | Ironclad A0. Insufficient damage, too many basics.
**Run 2**: Defeat Floor 9 (Terror Eel Elite) | Ironclad A0. Entered Elite at 35 HP. Vulnerable 99 made any hit lethal.
**Run 3**: Defeat Floor 9 (Terror Eel Elite) | Ironclad A0. Entered Elite at 41 HP (51%). Had good deck (Rage/Bloodletting/2xPommel/Shrug/BloodWall) + 3 potions. Got Eel to 16 HP at 1 HP but died. **CRITICAL PATHING ERROR**: Chose RestSite(6,3) which FORCED Elite path. Should have chosen Shop(6,2) which allowed avoiding Elite via (7,1)→(8,2) Monster route. Healing was less important than path flexibility.

## Enemy Knowledge
- **Living Fog**: 80 HP. Summons Gas Bombs (10 HP, 8 damage). Applies "Smoggy" (1 skill/turn). Minions die when leader dies. KILL LEADER ASAP. With Smoggy, prioritize attacks over skills.
- **Gas Bomb**: 10 HP minions, 8 damage. Die when leader dies.
- **Corpse Slug**: RavenousPower(4). When enemy dies, remaining slugs eat corpse → stunned + gain 4 Strength each. Chain-kill strategy works but last slug has MASSIVE Strength. Block T1 even if it delays chain - don't take 14 unblocked.
- **Sewer Clam**: 56 HP. Plating block (starts 8, decreases by 1/turn). Buffs Strength +4 repeatedly. Long fights = death. Need burst + Vulnerable. Bash through Plating is inefficient (8 dmg vs 8 block = 0 HP damage). Need to outpace Plating with multi-attack turns or Vulnerable.
- **Seapunk**: 45 HP. Moderate. Attacks + buffs Strength. Manageable.
- **Toadpole**: Buffs (Thorns +2, Strength). Kill the buffer first. Thorns = 2 per attack hit. Shrug It Off for block absorbs Thorns.
- **Sludge Spinner**: 37 HP. Attacks + applies Weak + buffs Strength. Kill fast.
- **Terror Eel (ELITE)**: 140 HP. ShriekPower(70) = STUNNED when first drops to ≤50% HP. VigorPower buffs next attack. Applies Vulnerable 99 via 2 debuff turns after stun. Post-Vuln attacks hit 25+ (displayed number INCLUDES your Vulnerability). STRATEGY: Rush to 70 HP → free stun turn → 2 debuff turns (free damage) → MUST block perfectly after Vuln99. Need ~68 damage in 4-5 turns to trigger stun, then finish remaining 70 HP with 2 free turns + careful blocking.

## Card Evaluation (Ironclad)
### Strong (Always Take):
- **Shrug It Off**: 8 block + draw for 1 energy. Best common skill.
- **Pommel Strike**: 9 damage + draw for 1 energy. Strict upgrade to Strike.
- **Rage**: 0 cost, +3 block per attack this turn. AMAZING with attack-heavy hands + Bloodletting.
- **Bloodletting**: 0 cost, +1 energy, -3 HP. Enables big turns. NEVER play at ≤3 HP.

### Situational:
- **Blood Wall**: 16 block for 2 energy + 2 HP. Efficient but HP cost dangerous at low HP. Good in healthy state.
- **Pillage**: 6 damage + draw until non-attack. Interesting with attack-heavy builds - could chain into more attacks.

### Skip:
- **Sword Boomerang**: 3x3 random. Unreliable.
- **Tremble**: Worse Vulnerable than Bash.
- **Molten Fist**: Exhaust = one-use. Skip.
- **Perfected Strike**: Trap card. Gets worse with Strike removal.
- **Setup Strike**: 7 damage + 2 temp Strength. Mediocre.
- **Bully**: 4 damage + bonus per Vulnerable. Too conditional.

### HIGH PRIORITY NEEDS:
- **Strength scaling**: Demon Form, Inflame, Limit Break, Spot Weakness - ANY permanent Strength source. ALL 3 RUNS lacked this.
- **AOE damage**: Multi-enemy fights are HP drains without it.
- **Uncommon/Rare damage**: Carnage, Uppercut, Clothesline, etc.
- **Card removal**: Remove Strikes at shops. 75g well spent.

## Potion Knowledge
- **Radiant Tincture**: "获得{Energy}。在你的下N个回合开始时，额外获得1能量。" Use T1 of hard fights. NOTE: Placeholder text unclear on exact energy amounts - don't over-rely on potion energy math.
- **Cure All**: "获得{Energy}。抽2张牌。" Draws + possible energy. Use for card access in critical moments.
- **Weak Potion**: 3 Weak. Reduces attacks 25%. Use T1 vs big hitters to reduce damage for 3 turns.
- **CRITICAL**: Potions are FREE actions. Always use BEFORE playing cards.

## Strategic Lessons (KEY - All 3 Runs)
### #1: PATHING IS MORE IMPORTANT THAN HEALING
- Run 3's fatal mistake: Chose RestSite over Shop when Shop path AVOIDED the Elite entirely. Always check where paths lead before choosing rest/shop/unknown.
- Rest that forces you into Elite > Shop that lets you avoid Elite.

### #2: HP Management
- All 3 runs died entering Elite at 35-41 HP (44-51%). Need 60%+ HP (48+ for 80 max).
- Use potions in regular fights to PRESERVE HP for Elite, not save them all.
- Living Fog + Corpse Slugs drained 39 HP in Run 3. Could have used Weak Potion on Corpse Slugs T1 to save 5-8 HP.

### #3: Avoid Forced Elites
- If a path forces you through an Elite with no alternative, DON'T take it unless you're at 70%+ HP with potions.
- Shop paths often branch more than Rest paths.

### #4: Block First, Damage Second at Low HP
- At ≤20 HP: ALWAYS block over damage. Period.
- At 20-40 HP: Block incoming fully, deal damage only with leftover energy.
- At 40+ HP: Can afford aggression if it speeds up kill.

### #5: Don't Be Greedy T1 Against Attackers
- Run 3 T1 vs Corpse Slugs: All-in damage, took 14 unblocked. Should have blocked + dealt less damage.
- Run 2 & 3 T1 vs Terror Eel: Went offensive, took 10-12+ unblocked.

### #6: Use Potions Earlier
- Weak Potion on Corpse Slug T1 saves ~5 HP over fight.
- Radiant Tincture on Sewer Clam (scaling enemy) could shorten fight by 2 turns = save 10+ HP.
- Entering Elite at higher HP is worth more than having potions at low HP.

## Combat Priorities (Turn-by-Turn)
1. Check incoming damage FIRST
2. Calculate: can I block all of it?
3. If HP ≤ 20: block is ALWAYS priority
4. If HP ≤ 40: block fully, damage with leftover
5. If enemy is buffing (no attack): go all-in on damage
6. Use Rage BEFORE attacks (0 cost)
7. Use Pommel Strike for draw before committing remaining energy
8. Bloodletting only when HP > 15
9. Blood Wall only when HP > 10
10. Save Bash for high-HP enemies where Vulnerable pays off over 2+ turns

## Deck Building Priority
1. Pommel Strike x2 early (replace Strikes)
2. Shrug It Off for defense + cycle
3. Strength scaling (CRITICAL NEED - 0/3 runs found any)
4. Rage for attack/defense synergy
5. Remove Strikes at shops (75g, very high priority)
6. Don't bloat past ~17 cards
7. Need more uncommon/rare damage cards

## Pathing Principles (REVISED - CRITICAL)
1. **CHECK ALL DOWNSTREAM PATHS** before choosing a room. A rest site that forces Elite is WORSE than a shop that avoids it.
2. Shop > Rest when: you have gold for removal AND shop path avoids Elite
3. Rest before Elite ONLY if you're already committed to Elite path
4. Don't take Elites below 60% HP
5. Use potions in hallway fights to preserve HP - don't hoard all for Elite
6. Ideal pre-Elite path: Monster → Monster → Shop(remove) → Rest → Elite
7. If possible, avoid Elites in Act 1 entirely until deck has scaling

# Slay the Spire 2 - Memory File

## Run Summaries
**Run 1**: Defeat Floor 9 (Sewer Clam) | Ironclad A0. Insufficient damage, too many basics.
**Run 2**: Defeat Floor 9 (Terror Eel Elite) | Ironclad A0. Entered Elite at 35 HP. Vulnerable 99 made any hit lethal.
**Run 3**: Defeat Floor 9 (Terror Eel Elite) | Ironclad A0. Entered Elite at 41 HP. PATHING ERROR forced Elite.
**Run 4**: Defeat Floor 17 (Waterfall Giant Boss) | Ironclad A0. Good pathing (avoided all Elites), decent 16-card deck with 3 powers (Vicious/Juggling/Stampede). Lost 25 HP rerolling event removal. Boss had 250 HP with escalating damage (10→15→25→30). Couldn't sustain both blocking and damage output. Lacked Strength scaling - attacks did 6-9 damage against 250 HP boss. **KEY FAILURE**: No Strength source in entire run. Powers were too slow/conditional without raw damage. Potions never activated despite repeated attempts (POTION command issue?).

## CRITICAL BUGS/MECHANICS
### POTION USAGE - MAJOR ISSUE IN RUN 4
- Potions repeatedly failed to activate across multiple turns. Tried POTION P1, P2, P3 many times.
- They stayed in inventory the ENTIRE boss fight despite multiple POTION commands.
- **THEORY**: Maybe potions that generate cards (Power Potion, Colorless Potion) require a selection step I'm not handling? Or maybe they can only be used one per line?
- **NEXT RUN**: Try using only ONE potion per action line. Use simple potions (Block, Weak, Vulnerable) that don't require choices.

## Enemy Knowledge
- **Living Fog**: 80 HP. Summons Gas Bombs (10 HP, 8 damage). Applies "Smoggy" (1 skill/turn). Minions die when leader dies. KILL LEADER ASAP.
- **Gas Bomb**: 10 HP minions, 8 damage. Die when leader dies.
- **Corpse Slug**: RavenousPower(4). When one dies, others eat corpse → stunned + gain 4 Strength. Chain-kill = free stun turns. Whirlwind excellent here to kill multiple simultaneously.
- **Sewer Clam**: 56 HP. Plating (starts 8, -1/turn). Buffs Strength +4 repeatedly. MUST kill fast. Vulnerable critical to break through Plating.
- **Seapunk**: 45 HP. Moderate. Manageable.
- **Toadpole**: Buffs (Thorns +2, Strength). Kill buffer first. Thorns = 2 per attack hit.
- **Sludge Spinner**: 37 HP. Attacks + Weak + Strength buffs. Kill fast.
- **Fossil Stalker**: 51 HP. SuckPower(3) = gains Strength when dealing UNBLOCKED damage. MUST block fully every turn or it snowballs. Patient fight - block first, damage with leftover.
- **Terror Eel (ELITE)**: 140 HP. Stuns at ≤50% HP. Applies Vulnerable 99 after stun. Must block perfectly post-Vuln.
- **Waterfall Giant (BOSS)**: 250 HP. SteamEruptionPower escalates each turn (+3 per turn). Pattern: Buff → Attack+Debuff+Buff → Attack+Buff → Heal+Buff → repeat with escalating damage (10→13→15→20→25→30+). Applies Weak and Vulnerable. **CRITICAL**: Damage escalates to 25-30+ by turn 8-10. MUST have Strength scaling or will be overwhelmed. Without scaling, ~8 damage/turn vs 250 HP = 30+ turns = impossible to survive escalating attacks.

## Card Evaluation (Ironclad)
### S-Tier (Always Take):
- **Shrug It Off**: 8 block + draw. Best common skill. Take 2-3 copies.
- **Pommel Strike**: 9 damage + draw. Strict Strike upgrade.
- **Battle Trance**: 0 cost, draw 3. Incredible hand reload. Play BEFORE Shrug (draw order matters).
- **Whirlwind**: X energy AOE. Amazing vs multi-enemy AND single target when dumping energy.

### A-Tier (Usually Take):
- **Headbutt**: 9 damage + tutor from discard. Great for recurring Bash/key cards.
- **Twin Strike**: 5×2 for 1 energy. Better than Strike, good with Juggling/Vulnerable.
- **Rage**: 0 cost, +3 block per attack. Amazing with attack-heavy hands.
- **Bloodletting**: 0 cost, +1 energy, -3 HP. Big turn enabler.

### B-Tier (Situational):
- **Stampede**: Free attack at end of turn. Decent but unreliable (may pick Whirlwind at 0 energy = wasted).
- **Juggling**: Copy of 3rd attack. Needs attack-dense hands to trigger consistently. Slow setup.
- **Vicious**: Draw on Vulnerable application. Only triggers with Bash - too narrow.
- **Blood Wall**: 16 block for 2 energy + 2 HP. Good when healthy.

### SKIP:
- **Bully, Tremble, Molten Fist, Perfected Strike, Setup Strike**: All bad.

### CRITICAL PRIORITY - STRENGTH SCALING:
- **ALL 4 RUNS** lacked permanent Strength. This is THE #1 reason for losing.
- Take ANY: Demon Form, Inflame, Limit Break, Spot Weakness, Fight Me (gives +2 Str)
- Without Strength, attacks do 6-9 damage. Boss has 250 HP. Math doesn't work.
- **Fight Me** (2 energy, 5×2 damage + 2 Strength, enemy gets 1 Str): SHOULD HAVE BOUGHT this at the shop for 76g instead of Shrug #3.

## Potion Knowledge
- **Weak Potion**: 3 Weak. Use T1 vs big attackers. Reduces 25% damage for 3 turns.
- **Vulnerable Potion**: Free Vuln application. Good with Vicious.
- **Block Potion**: Emergency block. Save for lethal turns.
- **Fysh Oil**: +1 Str, +1 Dex permanent in combat. Use T1 of boss/elite.
- **Power Potion / Colorless Potion**: Generate card choices. MAY REQUIRE SPECIAL HANDLING - failed to activate in Run 4. Try using alone on separate lines.
- **Energy Potion**: Extra energy. Use on big damage turns.

## Strategic Lessons

### #1: STRENGTH SCALING IS NON-NEGOTIABLE
- 4 runs, 0 Strength sources, 4 defeats. Without scaling, boss fights are unwinnable.
- Prioritize Strength cards over defense/utility. Even expensive ones (2 energy powers) are worth it.
- Buy Strength from shops even at premium prices.

### #2: PATHING
- Check ALL downstream paths before choosing rooms.
- Shop > Rest when you have gold AND shop avoids dangerous paths.
- Avoid Elites below 60% HP.
- Pre-boss: need Shop(buy) → Rest(heal) → Boss at near full HP.
- Run 4 pathing was good (avoided Elites, hit shops, rest before boss). Keep this approach.

### #3: EVENT REROLL TRAP
- Lost 25 HP (3+4+5+6+7) rerolling event to remove a Strike. Maximum 2-3 rerolls before HP cost exceeds benefit. Set HARD LIMIT: stop rerolling after 12 HP spent total.

### #4: HP MANAGEMENT
- Block fully vs scaling enemies (Fossil Stalker SuckPower, Sewer Clam Strength).
- Use Whirlwind to end multi-enemy fights fast (Corpse Slug simultaneous kill).
- Burning Blood (+6) helps but isn't enough to cover sloppy play.

### #5: POWER SETUP TIMING
- Boss free turns (Heal+Buff) are rare and precious. Play ALL powers on these turns.
- Don't play 3 powers over 3 turns - play damage/block powers together when safe.
- Run 4: Had Vicious, Juggling, Stampede but they took 4+ turns to set up. By then, boss was dealing 25+.

### #6: BOSS PREPARATION
- Need 15+ block/turn sustained AND 15+ damage/turn sustained for Waterfall Giant.
- With 3 energy: ideal is 1 block card (8-16) + 1 Strength-boosted attack (15+) per turn.
- Deck needs to average blocking incoming while still killing 250 HP in ~12 turns.

### #7: USE POTIONS PROACTIVELY
- Don't save all potions for boss. Use in hallway fights to preserve HP.
- Simple potions (Weak, Block) > Complex potions (Power, Colorless) due to activation issues.

## Combat Priorities
1. Check incoming damage FIRST
2. At ≤20 HP: block is ALWAYS priority - NO exceptions
3. At 20-40 HP: block fully, damage with leftover
4. At 40+ HP: can be aggressive if it shortens fight
5. Enemy buffing (no attack): go all-in on damage/setup
6. Play draw cards (Shrug, Battle Trance) BEFORE committing energy to maximize options
7. Battle Trance BEFORE Shrug (BT prevents draws; use Shrug draw first if both in hand)
8. Headbutt: always put Bash or Battle Trance on top unless specific need

## Deck Building Priority (REVISED)
1. **STRENGTH SCALING** - #1 priority above all else
2. Shrug It Off ×2-3 for defense + cycle
3. Pommel Strike / Twin Strike to replace Strikes
4. Battle Trance for hand reload
5. Whirlwind for AOE/energy dump
6. Remove Strikes at shops (75-100g)
7. Keep deck at 15-17 cards
8. Don't take conditional/slow powers without core scaling
[MEMORY SAVED]


# Slay the Spire 2 - Memory File

## Run Summaries
**Run 1**: Defeat Floor 9 (Sewer Clam) | Ironclad A0. Insufficient damage, too many basics.
**Run 2**: Defeat Floor 9 (Terror Eel Elite) | Ironclad A0. Entered Elite at 35 HP. Vulnerable 99 made any hit lethal.
**Run 3**: Defeat Floor 9 (Terror Eel Elite) | Ironclad A0. Entered Elite at 41 HP. PATHING ERROR forced Elite.
**Run 4**: Defeat Floor 17 (Waterfall Giant Boss) | Ironclad A0. Good pathing (avoided all Elites), decent 16-card deck with 3 powers (Vicious/Juggling/Stampede). Lost 25 HP rerolling event removal. Boss had 250 HP with escalating damage (10→15→25→30). Couldn't sustain both blocking and damage output. Lacked Strength scaling - attacks did 6-9 damage against 250 HP boss. **KEY FAILURE**: No Strength source in entire run. Powers were too slow/conditional without raw damage. Potions never activated despite repeated attempts (POTION command issue?).

## CRITICAL BUGS/MECHANICS
### POTION USAGE - MAJOR ISSUE IN RUN 4
- Potions repeatedly failed to activate across multiple turns. Tried POTION P1, P2, P3 many times.
- They stayed in inventory the ENTIRE boss fight despite multiple POTION commands.
- **THEORY**: Maybe potions that generate cards (Power Potion, Colorless Potion) require a selection step I'm not handling? Or maybe they can only be used one per line?
- **NEXT RUN**: Try using only ONE potion per action line. Use simple potions (Block, Weak, Vulnerable) that don't require choices.

## Enemy Knowledge
- **Living Fog**: 80 HP. Summons Gas Bombs (10 HP, 8 damage). Applies "Smoggy" (1 skill/turn). Minions die when leader dies. KILL LEADER ASAP.
- **Gas Bomb**: 10 HP minions, 8 damage. Die when leader dies.
- **Corpse Slug**: RavenousPower(4). When one dies, others eat corpse → stunned + gain 4 Strength. Chain-kill = free stun turns. Whirlwind excellent here to kill multiple simultaneously.
- **Sewer Clam**: 56 HP. Plating (starts 8, -1/turn). Buffs Strength +4 repeatedly. MUST kill fast. Vulnerable critical to break through Plating.
- **Seapunk**: 45 HP. Moderate. Manageable.
- **Toadpole**: Buffs (Thorns +2, Strength). Kill buffer first. Thorns = 2 per attack hit.
- **Sludge Spinner**: 37 HP. Attacks + Weak + Strength buffs. Kill fast.
- **Fossil Stalker**: 51 HP. SuckPower(3) = gains Strength when dealing UNBLOCKED damage. MUST block fully every turn or it snowballs. Patient fight - block first, damage with leftover.
- **Terror Eel (ELITE)**: 140 HP. Stuns at ≤50% HP. Applies Vulnerable 99 after stun. Must block perfectly post-Vuln.
- **Waterfall Giant (BOSS)**: 250 HP. SteamEruptionPower escalates each turn (+3 per turn). Pattern: Buff → Attack+Debuff+Buff → Attack+Buff → Heal+Buff → repeat with escalating damage (10→13→15→20→25→30+). Applies Weak and Vulnerable. **CRITICAL**: Damage escalates to 25-30+ by turn 8-10. MUST have Strength scaling or will be overwhelmed. Without scaling, ~8 damage/turn vs 250 HP = 30+ turns = impossible to survive escalating attacks.

## Card Evaluation (Ironclad)
### S-Tier (Always Take):
- **Shrug It Off**: 8 block + draw. Best common skill. Take 2-3 copies.
- **Pommel Strike**: 9 damage + draw. Strict Strike upgrade.
- **Battle Trance**: 0 cost, draw 3. Incredible hand reload. Play BEFORE Shrug (draw order matters).
- **Whirlwind**: X energy AOE. Amazing vs multi-enemy AND single target when dumping energy.

### A-Tier (Usually Take):
- **Headbutt**: 9 damage + tutor from discard. Great for recurring Bash/key cards.
- **Twin Strike**: 5×2 for 1 energy. Better than Strike, good with Juggling/Vulnerable.
- **Rage**: 0 cost, +3 block per attack. Amazing with attack-heavy hands.
- **Bloodletting**: 0 cost, +1 energy, -3 HP. Big turn enabler.

### B-Tier (Situational):
- **Stampede**: Free attack at end of turn. Decent but unreliable (may pick Whirlwind at 0 energy = wasted).
- **Juggling**: Copy of 3rd attack. Needs attack-dense hands to trigger consistently. Slow setup.
- **Vicious**: Draw on Vulnerable application. Only triggers with Bash - too narrow.
- **Blood Wall**: 16 block for 2 energy + 2 HP. Good when healthy.

### SKIP:
- **Bully, Tremble, Molten Fist, Perfected Strike, Setup Strike**: All bad.

### CRITICAL PRIORITY - STRENGTH SCALING:
- **ALL 4 RUNS** lacked permanent Strength. This is THE #1 reason for losing.
- Take ANY: Demon Form, Inflame, Limit Break, Spot Weakness, Fight Me (gives +2 Str)
- Without Strength, attacks do 6-9 damage. Boss has 250 HP. Math doesn't work.
- **Fight Me** (2 energy, 5×2 damage + 2 Strength, enemy gets 1 Str): SHOULD HAVE BOUGHT this at the shop for 76g instead of Shrug #3.

## Potion Knowledge
- **Weak Potion**: 3 Weak. Use T1 vs big attackers. Reduces 25% damage for 3 turns.
- **Vulnerable Potion**: Free Vuln application. Good with Vicious.
- **Block Potion**: Emergency block. Save for lethal turns.
- **Fysh Oil**: +1 Str, +1 Dex permanent in combat. Use T1 of boss/elite.
- **Power Potion / Colorless Potion**: Generate card choices. MAY REQUIRE SPECIAL HANDLING - failed to activate in Run 4. Try using alone on separate lines.
- **Energy Potion**: Extra energy. Use on big damage turns.

## Strategic Lessons

### #1: STRENGTH SCALING IS NON-NEGOTIABLE
- 4 runs, 0 Strength sources, 4 defeats. Without scaling, boss fights are unwinnable.
- Prioritize Strength cards over defense/utility. Even expensive ones (2 energy powers) are worth it.
- Buy Strength from shops even at premium prices.

### #2: PATHING
- Check ALL downstream paths before choosing rooms.
- Shop > Rest when you have gold AND shop avoids dangerous paths.
- Avoid Elites below 60% HP.
- Pre-boss: need Shop(buy) → Rest(heal) → Boss at near full HP.
- Run 4 pathing was good (avoided Elites, hit shops, rest before boss). Keep this approach.

### #3: EVENT REROLL TRAP
- Lost 25 HP (3+4+5+6+7) rerolling event to remove a Strike. Maximum 2-3 rerolls before HP cost exceeds benefit. Set HARD LIMIT: stop rerolling after 12 HP spent total.

### #4: HP MANAGEMENT
- Block fully vs scaling enemies (Fossil Stalker SuckPower, Sewer Clam Strength).
- Use Whirlwind to end multi-enemy fights fast (Corpse Slug simultaneous kill).
- Burning Blood (+6) helps but isn't enough to cover sloppy play.

### #5: POWER SETUP TIMING
- Boss free turns (Heal+Buff) are rare and precious. Play ALL powers on these turns.
- Don't play 3 powers over 3 turns - play damage/block powers together when safe.
- Run 4: Had Vicious, Juggling, Stampede but they took 4+ turns to set up. By then, boss was dealing 25+.

### #6: BOSS PREPARATION
- Need 15+ block/turn sustained AND 15+ damage/turn sustained for Waterfall Giant.
- With 3 energy: ideal is 1 block card (8-16) + 1 Strength-boosted attack (15+) per turn.
- Deck needs to average blocking incoming while still killing 250 HP in ~12 turns.

### #7: USE POTIONS PROACTIVELY
- Don't save all potions for boss. Use in hallway fights to preserve HP.
- Simple potions (Weak, Block) > Complex potions (Power, Colorless) due to activation issues.

## Combat Priorities
1. Check incoming damage FIRST
2. At ≤20 HP: block is ALWAYS priority - NO exceptions
3. At 20-40 HP: block fully, damage with leftover
4. At 40+ HP: can be aggressive if it shortens fight
5. Enemy buffing (no attack): go all-in on damage/setup
6. Play draw cards (Shrug, Battle Trance) BEFORE committing energy to maximize options
7. Battle Trance BEFORE Shrug (BT prevents draws; use Shrug draw first if both in hand)
8. Headbutt: always put Bash or Battle Trance on top unless specific need

## Deck Building Priority (REVISED)
1. **STRENGTH SCALING** - #1 priority above all else
2. Shrug It Off ×2-3 for defense + cycle
3. Pommel Strike / Twin Strike to replace Strikes
4. Battle Trance for hand reload
5. Whirlwind for AOE/energy dump
6. Remove Strikes at shops (75-100g)
7. Keep deck at 15-17 cards
8. Don't take conditional/slow powers without core scaling
